<dl><dt><a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a></dt></dl></div></div></td>
</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-below" style="padding-top:0.15em;">
<a href="/wiki/Social_anthropology" title="Social anthropology">Social</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cultural_anthropology" title="Cultural anthropology">cultural anthropology</a></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Anthropology_of_religion" title="Template:Anthropology of religion"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Anthropology_of_religion" title="Template talk:Anthropology of religion"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Anthropology_of_religion&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>A <b>ritual</b> is a sequence of activities involving <a href="/wiki/Gesture" title="Gesture">gestures</a>, words, actions, or objects, performed according to a set sequence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Rituals may be prescribed by the <a href="/wiki/Tradition" title="Tradition">traditions</a> of a <a href="/wiki/Community" title="Community">community</a>, including a religious community. Rituals are characterized, but not defined, by formalism, traditionalism, invariance, rule-governance, sacral symbolism, and performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBell1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsritualperspectiv00bellpagen154_138]–169_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBell1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsritualperspectiv00bellpagen154_138]–169-3">[3]</a></sup>
</p><p>Rituals are a feature of all known human societies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> They include not only the <a href="/wiki/Worship" title="Worship">worship</a> rites and <a href="/wiki/Sacrament" title="Sacrament">sacraments</a> of organized religions and <a href="/wiki/Cult" title="Cult">cults</a>, but also <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rites_of_passage" title="Rites of passage">rites of passage</a>, atonement and <a href="/wiki/Ritual_purification" title="Ritual purification">purification rites</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oaths_of_allegiance" title="Oaths of allegiance">oaths of allegiance</a>, dedication ceremonies, <a href="/wiki/Coronation" title="Coronation">coronations</a> and presidential <a href="/wiki/Inauguration" title="Inauguration">inaugurations</a>, marriages, funerals and more. Even common actions like <a href="/wiki/Handshake" title="Handshake">hand-shaking</a> and saying "<a href="/wiki/Hello" title="Hello">hello</a>" may be termed as <i>rituals</i>.
</p><p>The field of ritual studies has seen a number of conflicting definitions of the term. One given by Kyriakidis is that a ritual is an outsider's or "<a href="/wiki/Emic_and_etic" title="Emic and etic">etic</a>" category for a set activity (or set of actions) that, to the outsider, seems irrational, non-contiguous, or illogical. The term can be used also by the insider or "<a href="/wiki/Emic_and_etic" title="Emic and etic">emic</a>" performer as an acknowledgement that this activity can be seen as such by the uninitiated onlooker.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p><span class="anchor" id="Psychology"></span>
In <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">psychology</a>, the term <i>ritual</i> is sometimes used in a technical sense for a repetitive behavior systematically used by a person to neutralize or prevent anxiety; it can be a symptom of <a href="/wiki/Obsessive%E2%80%93compulsive_disorder" title="Obsessive–compulsive disorder">obsessive–compulsive disorder</a> but obsessive-compulsive ritualistic behaviors are generally isolated activities.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ritual&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The English word <i>ritual</i> derives from the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i>ritualis,</i> "that which pertains to <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/rite" title="wikt:rite">rite</a> <i>(<a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_ancient_Roman_religion#ritus" title="Glossary of ancient Roman religion">ritus</a></i>)". In Roman <a href="/wiki/Roman_law" title="Roman law">juridical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_ancient_Rome" title="Religion in ancient Rome">religious</a> usage, <i>ritus</i> was the proven way <i>(<a href="/wiki/Mos_maiorum" title="Mos maiorum">mos</a>)</i> of doing something,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> or "correct performance, custom".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The original concept of <i>ritus</i> may be related to the <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rta" title="Rta">ṛtá</a></i> ("visible order)" in <a href="/wiki/Historical_Vedic_religion" title="Historical Vedic religion">Vedic religion</a>, "the lawful and regular order of the normal, and therefore proper, natural and true structure of cosmic, worldly, human and ritual events".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The word "ritual" is first recorded in English in 1570, and came into use in the 1600s to mean "the prescribed order of performing religious services" or more particularly a book of these prescriptions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Characteristics">Characteristics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ritual&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Characteristics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><span class="anchor" id="actions"></span>
There are hardly any limits to the kind of actions that may be incorporated into a ritual. The rites of past and present societies have typically involved special gestures and words, recitation of fixed texts, performance of special <a href="/wiki/Music" title="Music">music</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singing" title="Singing">songs</a> or <a href="/wiki/Dance" title="Dance">dances</a>, processions, manipulation of certain objects, use of special dresses, consumption of special <a href="/wiki/Food" title="Food">food</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drink" title="Drink">drink</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Entheogen" title="Entheogen">drugs</a>, and much more.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETolbert1990a_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETolbert1990a-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETolbert1990b_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETolbert1990b-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilce2006_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilce2006-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Catherine_Bell_(religious_studies_scholar)" title="Catherine Bell (religious studies scholar)">Catherine Bell</a> argues that rituals can be characterized by formalism, traditionalism, invariance, rule-governance, sacral symbolism and performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBell1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsritualperspectiv00bellpagen154_138]-169_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBell1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsritualperspectiv00bellpagen154_138]-169-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formalism">Formalism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ritual&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Formalism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IteMissaEst.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="357" data-file-width="533" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/IteMissaEst.jpg/220px-IteMissaEst.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/IteMissaEst.jpg/330px-IteMissaEst.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/IteMissaEst.jpg/440px-IteMissaEst.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IteMissaEst.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The use of Latin in a <a href="/wiki/Tridentine_Mass" title="Tridentine Mass">Tridentine Catholic Mass</a> is an example of a "restricted code".</div></div></div>
<p>Ritual utilizes a limited and rigidly organized set of expressions which <a href="/wiki/Anthropologist" title="Anthropologist">anthropologists</a> call a "restricted code" (in opposition to a more open "elaborated code"). Maurice Bloch argues that ritual obliges participants to use this formal oratorical style, which is limited in intonation, syntax, vocabulary, loudness, and fixity of order. In adopting this style, ritual leaders' speech becomes more style than content. Because this formal speech limits what can be said, it induces "acceptance, compliance, or at least forbearance with regard to any overt challenge". Bloch argues that this form of ritual communication makes rebellion impossible and revolution the only feasible alternative. Ritual tends to support traditional forms of social hierarchy and authority, and maintains the assumptions on which the authority is based from challenge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBell1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsritualperspectiv00bellpagen155_139]–140_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBell1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsritualperspectiv00bellpagen155_139]–140-14">[14]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditionalism">Traditionalism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ritual&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Traditionalism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_First_Thanksgiving_cph.3g04961.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1946" data-file-width="3050" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/The_First_Thanksgiving_cph.3g04961.jpg/220px-The_First_Thanksgiving_cph.3g04961.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/The_First_Thanksgiving_cph.3g04961.jpg/330px-The_First_Thanksgiving_cph.3g04961.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/The_First_Thanksgiving_cph.3g04961.jpg/440px-The_First_Thanksgiving_cph.3g04961.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_First_Thanksgiving_cph.3g04961.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The First Thanksgiving 1621</i>, oil on canvas by <a href="/wiki/Jean_Leon_Gerome_Ferris" title="Jean Leon Gerome Ferris">Jean Leon Gerome Ferris</a> (1863–1930). The painting shows common misconceptions about the event that persist to modern times: Pilgrims did not wear such outfits, and the Wampanoag are dressed in the style of <a href="/wiki/Plains_Indians" title="Plains Indians">Plains Indians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Rituals appeal to tradition and are generally continued to repeat historical precedent, religious rite, <a href="/wiki/Mores" title="Mores">mores</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Ceremony" title="Ceremony">ceremony</a> accurately. Traditionalism varies from formalism in that the ritual may not be formal yet still makes an appeal to the historical trend. An example is the American Thanksgiving dinner, which may not be formal, yet is ostensibly based on an event from the early Puritan settlement of America. Historians <a href="/wiki/Eric_Hobsbawm" title="Eric Hobsbawm">Eric Hobsbawm</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terrence_Ranger" title="Terrence Ranger">Terrence Ranger</a> have argued that many of these are <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Invented_traditions" title="Invented traditions">invented traditions</a></i>, such as the rituals of the British monarchy, which invoke "thousand year-old tradition" but whose actual form originate in the late nineteenth century, to some extent reviving earlier forms, in this case medieval, that had been discontinued in the meantime. Thus, the appeal to history is important rather than accurate historical transmission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBell1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsritualperspectiv00bellpagen161_145]–150_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBell1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsritualperspectiv00bellpagen161_145]–150-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Invariance">Invariance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ritual&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Invariance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Catherine_Bell_(religious_studies_scholar)" title="Catherine Bell (religious studies scholar)">Catherine Bell</a> states that ritual is also invariant, implying careful choreography. This is less an appeal to traditionalism than a striving for timeless repetition. The key to invariance is bodily discipline, as in monastic prayer and meditation meant to mold dispositions and moods. This bodily discipline is frequently performed in unison, by groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBell1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsritualperspectiv00bellpagen168_152]–153_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBell1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsritualperspectiv00bellpagen168_152]–153-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rule-governance">Rule-governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ritual&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Rule-governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Rituals tend to be governed by rules, a feature somewhat like formalism. Rules impose norms on the chaos of behavior, either defining the outer limits of what is acceptable or choreographing each move. Individuals are held to communally approved customs that evoke a legitimate communal authority that can constrain the possible outcomes. Historically, war in most societies has been bound by highly ritualized constraints that limit the legitimate means by which war was waged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBell1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsritualperspectiv00bellpagen171_155]_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBell1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsritualperspectiv00bellpagen171_155]-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sacral_symbolism">Sacral symbolism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ritual&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Sacral symbolism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ritual_Practitioner_on_Inwangsan_Mountain_(Detail).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4896" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Ritual_Practitioner_on_Inwangsan_Mountain_%28Detail%29.jpg/220px-Ritual_Practitioner_on_Inwangsan_Mountain_%28Detail%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Ritual_Practitioner_on_Inwangsan_Mountain_%28Detail%29.jpg/330px-Ritual_Practitioner_on_Inwangsan_Mountain_%28Detail%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Ritual_Practitioner_on_Inwangsan_Mountain_%28Detail%29.jpg/440px-Ritual_Practitioner_on_Inwangsan_Mountain_%28Detail%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ritual_Practitioner_on_Inwangsan_Mountain_(Detail).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ritual practitioner on Inwangsan Mountain, Seoul South Korea</div></div></div>
<p>Activities appealing to supernatural beings are easily considered rituals, although the appeal may be quite indirect, expressing only a generalized belief in the existence of the sacred demanding a human response. National flags, for example, may be considered more than signs representing a country. The flag stands for larger symbols such as freedom, democracy, free enterprise or national superiority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBell1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsritualperspectiv00bellpagen172_156]_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBell1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsritualperspectiv00bellpagen172_156]-19">[19]</a></sup> Anthropologist Sherry Ortner writes that the flag
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>does not encourage reflection on the logical relations among these ideas, nor on the logical consequences of them as they are played out in social actuality, over time and history. On the contrary, the flag encourages a sort of all-or-nothing allegiance to the whole package, best summed [by] 'Our flag, love it or leave.'<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Particular objects become sacral symbols through a process of <a href="/wiki/Consecration" title="Consecration">consecration</a> which effectively creates the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sacred-profane_dichotomy" title="Sacred-profane dichotomy">sacred</a> by setting it apart from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sacred-profane_dichotomy" title="Sacred-profane dichotomy">profane</a>. Boy Scouts and the armed forces in any country teach the official ways of folding, saluting and raising the flag, thus emphasizing that the flag should never be treated as just a piece of cloth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBell1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsritualperspectiv00bellpagen172_156]–57_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBell1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsritualperspectiv00bellpagen172_156]–57-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performance">Performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ritual&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The performance of ritual creates a theatrical-like frame around the activities, symbols and events that shape participant's experience and cognitive ordering of the world, simplifying the chaos of life and imposing a more or less coherent system of categories of meaning onto it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBell1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsritualperspectiv00bellpagen172_156]–157_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBell1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsritualperspectiv00bellpagen172_156]–157-22">[22]</a></sup> As Barbara Myerhoff put it, "not only is seeing believing, doing is believing."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Genres">Genres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ritual&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Genres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>For simplicity's sake, the range of diverse rituals can be divided into categories with common characteristics, generally falling into one three major categories:
</p>
<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rites_of_passage" title="Rites of passage">rites of passage</a>, generally changing an individual's social status;</li>
<li>communal rites, whether of <a href="/wiki/Worship" title="Worship">worship</a>, where a community comes together to worship, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jew" title="Jew">Jewish</a> <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">synagogue</a> or <a href="/wiki/Mass_(liturgy)" title="Mass (liturgy)">Mass</a>, or of another character, such as <a href="/wiki/Fertility_rite" title="Fertility rite">fertility rites</a> and certain non-religious <a href="/wiki/Festival" title="Festival">festivals</a>;</li>
<li>rites of personal devotion, where an individual worships, including prayer and <a href="/wiki/Pilgrimage" title="Pilgrimage">pilgrimages</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pledge_of_allegiance" title="Pledge of allegiance">pledges of allegiance</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Engagement" title="Engagement">promises to wed someone</a>.</li></ul>
<p>However, rituals can fall in more than one category or genre, and may be grouped in a variety of other ways. For example, the anthropologist <a href="/wiki/Victor_Turner" title="Victor Turner">Victor Turner</a> writes:
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Rituals may be seasonal, <abbr style="text-decoration:none;border-bottom:1px dotted black;margin-bottom:1px;" title="hallowing a culturally defined moment of change in the climatic cycle or the inauguration of an activity such as planting, harvesting, or moving from winter to summer pasture;">...</abbr> or they may be contingent, held in response to an individual or collective crisis. <abbr style="text-decoration:none;border-bottom:1px dotted black;margin-bottom:1px;" title="quote text omitted">...</abbr> Other classes of rituals include divinatory rituals; ceremonies performed by political authorities to ensure the health and fertility of human beings, animals, and crops in their territories; initiation into priesthoods devoted to certain deities, into religious associations, or into secret societies; and those accompanying the daily offering of food and libations to deities or ancestral spirits or both.</p><div class="templatequotecite">— <cite><a href="#CITEREFTurner1973">Turner (1973)</a></cite></div></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rites_of_passage">Rites of passage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ritual&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Rites of passage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E6%98%8E%E5%88%B6%E5%86%A0%E7%A6%AE.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="760" data-file-width="765" decoding="async" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/%E6%98%8E%E5%88%B6%E5%86%A0%E7%A6%AE.jpg/220px-%E6%98%8E%E5%88%B6%E5%86%A0%E7%A6%AE.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/%E6%98%8E%E5%88%B6%E5%86%A0%E7%A6%AE.jpg/330px-%E6%98%8E%E5%88%B6%E5%86%A0%E7%A6%AE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/%E6%98%8E%E5%88%B6%E5%86%A0%E7%A6%AE.jpg/440px-%E6%98%8E%E5%88%B6%E5%86%A0%E7%A6%AE.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E6%98%8E%E5%88%B6%E5%86%A0%E7%A6%AE.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Guan_Li" title="Guan Li">"capping" ceremony</a> is one of the principle rites of the <a href="/wiki/Confucian_ritual_religion" title="Confucian ritual religion">Confucian ritual religion</a>, alongside marriage, mourning rites, and sacrificial rituals</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rites_of_passage" title="Rites of passage">Rites of passage</a></div>
<p>A rite of passage is a ritual event that marks a person's transition from one <a href="/wiki/Social_status" title="Social status">status</a> to another, including <a href="/wiki/Adoption" title="Adoption">adoption</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baptism" title="Baptism">baptism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coming_of_age" title="Coming of age">coming of age</a>, <a href="/wiki/Graduation" title="Graduation">graduation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inauguration" title="Inauguration">inauguration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Engagement" title="Engagement">engagement</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">marriage</a>. Rites of passage may also include <a href="/wiki/Initiation" title="Initiation">initiation</a> into groups not tied to a formal stage of life such as a <a href="/wiki/Fraternity" title="Fraternity">fraternity</a>. <a href="/wiki/Arnold_van_Gennep" title="Arnold van Gennep">Arnold van Gennep</a> stated that rites of passage are marked by three stages:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBell1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsritualperspectiv00bellpagen110_94]_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBell1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsritualperspectiv00bellpagen110_94]-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>1. Separation</dt>
<dd>Wherein the initiates are separated from their old identities through physical and symbolic means.</dd></dl>
<dl><dt>2. Transition</dt>
<dd>Wherein the initiated are "betwixt and between". <a href="/wiki/Victor_Turner" title="Victor Turner">Victor Turner</a> argued that this stage is marked by <a href="/wiki/Liminality" title="Liminality">liminality</a>, a condition of ambiguity or disorientation in which initiates have been stripped of their old identities, but have not yet acquired their new one. Turner states that "the attributes of <a href="/wiki/Liminality" title="Liminality">liminality</a> or of liminal <i><a href="/wiki/Persona" title="Persona">personae</a></i> ("threshold people") are necessarily ambiguous".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner196995_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner196995-25">[25]</a></sup> In this stage of liminality or "anti-structure" (<a href="#Structure_and_anti-structure">see below</a>), the initiates' role ambiguity creates a sense of <a href="/wiki/Communitas" title="Communitas">communitas</a> or emotional bond of community between them. This stage may be marked by ritual ordeals or ritual training.</dd></dl>
<dl><dt>3. Incorporation</dt>
<dd>Wherein the initiates are symbolically confirmed in their new identity and community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner196997_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner196997-26">[26]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rites_of_affliction">Rites of affliction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ritual&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Rites of affliction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Shamanism" title="Shamanism">Shamanism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Exorcism" title="Exorcism">Exorcism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ritual_purification" title="Ritual purification">Ritual purification</a></div>
<p>Anthropologist Victor Turner defines rites of affliction actions that seek to mitigate spirits or supernatural forces that inflict humans with bad luck, illness, gynecological troubles, physical injuries, and other such misfortunes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner1973_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner1973-27">[27]</a></sup> These rites may include forms of spirit <a href="/wiki/Divination" title="Divination">divination</a> (consulting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oracles" title="Oracles">oracles</a>) to establish causes—and rituals that heal, purify, exorcise, and protect. The misfortune experienced may include individual health, but also broader climate-related issues such as drought or plagues of insects. Healing rites performed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shamans" title="Shamans">shamans</a> frequently identify social disorder as the cause, and make the restoration of social relationships the cure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner19679ff_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner19679ff-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p><p>Turner uses the example of the Isoma ritual among the Ndembu of northwestern <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> to illustrate. The Isoma rite of affliction is used to cure a childless woman of infertility. Infertility is the result of a "structural tension between <a href="/wiki/Matrilineality" title="Matrilineality">matrilineal</a> descent and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virilocality" title="Virilocality">virilocal</a> marriage" (i.e., the tension a woman feels between her mother's family, to whom she owes allegiance, and her husband's family among whom she must live). "It is because the woman has come too closely in touch with the 'man's side' in her marriage that her dead matrikin have impaired her fertility." To correct the balance of matrilinial descent and marriage, the Isoma ritual dramatically placates the deceased spirits by requiring the woman to reside with her mother's kin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner196920–21_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner196920–21-29">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>Shamanic and other ritual may effect a psychotherapeutic cure, leading anthropologists such as Jane Atkinson to theorize how. Atkinson argues that the effectiveness of a shamanic ritual for an individual may depend upon a wider audiences acknowledging the shaman's power, which may lead to the shaman placing greater emphasis on engaging the audience than in the healing of the patient.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Death.2C_mourning.2C_and_funerary_rites"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Death,_mourning,_and_funerary_rites">Death, mourning, and funerary rites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ritual&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Death, mourning, and funerary rites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Funeral" title="Funeral">Funeral</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+link+.ambox{margin-top:-1px}html body.mediawiki .mw-parser-output .ambox.mbox-small-left{margin:4px 1em 4px 0;overflow:hidden;width:238px;border-collapse:collapse;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em}.mw-parser-output .ambox-speedy{border-left:10px solid #b32424;background-color:#fee7e6}.mw-parser-output .ambox-delete{border-left:10px solid #b32424}.mw-parser-output .ambox-content{border-left:10px solid #f28500}.mw-parser-output .ambox-style{border-left:10px solid #fc3}.mw-parser-output .ambox-move{border-left:10px solid #9932cc}.mw-parser-output .ambox-protection{border-left:10px solid #a2a9b1}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-text{border:none;padding:0.25em
